      <article class="entry clearfix post-10453 post type-post status-publish format-standard hentry category-arthritis-joint-pain" id="post-10453">
       <div class="updated">
        Last Modified: November 24, 2014
       </div>
       <div class="post_content clearfix">
        <h1 class="title">
         <span class="entry-title">
          What is the Connection Between Arthritis and Joint Pain
         </span>
        </h1>
        <span class="vcard author">
         <span class="fn">
          <div class="vcard author">
           <div class="fn">
            <div style="float:left;width:100px;margin:0 10px 0 0">
             <a href="https://plus.google.com/107543701530457039041/posts" rel="publisher">
              <img alt="Janice Carson" src="https://www.jointhealthmagazine.com/wp-content/themes/Lucid/images/janice-carson.png" title="Janice Carson"/>
             </a>
             <span class="fn-authr">
              Janice Carson
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <p>
           When someone experiences joint pain, the first thing that comes to mind is arthritis. Why is it common knowledge that arthritis causes joint pain? Does it really? What is the connection between the disease and its symptoms?
          </p>
          <h2>
           Psoriatic Arthritis and Joint Pain
          </h2>
          <p>
           <img alt="What is the Connection Between Arthritis and Joint Pain" src="https://www.jointhealthmagazine.com/prod-images/arthritis-and-joint-pain.jpg" title="What is the Connection Between Arthritis and Joint Pain"/>
           Psoriatic arthritis is chronic inflammation. It is affected by the immune system, genetic and environmental factors. The most common symptoms of psoriatic arthritis are joint inflammation and skin problems. The joint inflammation can happen in the knees, hands, wrists, ankles, lower back and feet. The main connection between
           <b>
            arthritis and joint pain
           </b>
           lies on the symptom joint inflammation. If the joints are inflamed, there will be pain and discomfort.
          </p>
          <p>
           People who have psoriasis have a 30% more chance of developing psoriatic
           <a href="/arthritis-joint-pain-relief.html" title="arthritis and joint pain">
            arthritis and joint Pain
           </a>
           . This can mostly happen among people age 30-50. It can happen to both men and women. The symptoms of psoriasis happen first and the development of psoriatic arthritis can come years later. But, there are cases when the arthritis happens first. Since cases are unique from each other, it will be best to consult a physician.
          </p>
          <h2>
           Warning Signs to Look Out For
          </h2>
          <p>
           How do you know if you may have psoriatic arthritis already? A sign is when the joints are tender and swollen. This can happen in the hinge joints in the hands and feet. Another sign is when the fingers and toes look swollen like sausages. Inflammation of the tendons is a sign too. If you feel stiffness, fatigue and reduced range of motion, you may have psoriatic arthritis.
          </p>
          <h2>
           The Cause and Treatment
          </h2>
          <p>
           The exact
           <em>
            cause of psoriatic arthritis and joint pain
           </em>
           is not yet determined but experts believe that the immune system, environmental and genetic factors contribute to the diseases development. This was discovered when a closer look on the immune system was done. There were similar things happening on a psoriatic skin and joint. The immune system acts abnormally by being too overactive. This results in joint inflammation and inflammation of the surrounding tissues.
          </p>
          <p>
           In treating this condition, it is best to always get an early diagnosis. Watch out for the warning signs and consult a physician right away to get the appropriate treatment. Treatment goals should relieve pain, reduce inflammation, regain range of motion, prevent joint and tissue damage and help the joints function properly once again. The doctor can also give medication to ease the pain.
          </p>
          <p>
           Furthermore, to prevent
           <span style="text-decoration: underline;">
            joint pain and inflammation
           </span>
           , eating a healthy diet is very important. Taking care of the joints should be done too. As you age, try to exert lesser effort when doing manual tasks to prevent overexertion of joints. On the other hand, if your body is bound to have arthritis, the best way to avoid joint pain is to do some therapy and strengthen the joints once again.
          </p>
         </span>
        </span>

         <div class="addtitle">

           <figure>
            <a href="https://www.jointhealthmagazine.com/flexoplex.html">
             <img alt="Flexoplex" src="https://www.jointhealthmagazine.com/wp-content/themes/Lucid/images/p-flexoplex.jpg"/>

          <div class="desc_col">
           <div class="star">
            <strong>
